    <li> The older that I&#x27;ve gotten, the more facial hair I seem to be getting. This is not something that is very exciting to me. I&#x27;ve tried waxing, plucking and even shaving the few hairs that poke through. While effective, these methods can often prove to be painful and time consuming. With this facial hair remover, I was able to easily remove my facial hair with minimal pain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After ordering, this product arrived two days later. After removing it from the packaging, you see the the long spiral coil with two handles on either end. To use this facial hair remover, you hold the coil against your skin, stretch it apart, let the coil fold back into themselves and pull the coil away from your face. When you look down at the coil, you see the hairs between the coils. Simply stretching the coils back apart empties the hair from the coils. Then, you are able to start again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Despite the fact that you are basically plucking a lot of the hair out at one time, I found this to not be very painful.     <li> I almost never write reviews, but after using my new Bellabe for the first time today, I have to rate it FIVE STARS! I am a post-menopausal woman who has plenty of long, blonde, silky hair -- too bad it&#x27;s all over my face and neck. Along with a few dark and brittle ones that pop up on the chin and moustache. I was in despair when I went online and started researching. Bellabe sounded like a dream come true, and, feeling optimistic, I ordered the two-pack. Ladies, you won&#x27;t believe this thing!!! I was worried because if it didn&#x27;t work, I didn&#x27;t know what I was going to do about the facial hair. Plus, I am usually a total klutz with tools of any kind. Once I got the hang of it, it was actually fun ... I know, I know, how fun can it be to rip your unwanted hair out by the roots? But it was strangely addictive, like popping those plastic bubbles on shipping wrap. The best part of all -- I was done in less than 15 minutes and my face and neck feels totally smooth and soft. I had minimal redness which disappeared in less than 20 minutes. The Bellabe grabbed all the hairs except for the very shortest, finest ones, which gives a much more natural appearance. It looks like I have natural &amp;#34;peach fuzz&amp;#34; like I had before menopause. I will never be without this tool again. Here are a few tips that they don&#x27;t mention in the directions: 1. The handles are printed with a number 1 on one end and a number 2 on the other. I had no idea why, so I experimented and found out that the tool works if you hold the 1 in your left hand and the 2 in your right hand, and twist the handles inward (fingers toward each other, toward the center of the inverted U shape.) 2. Be certain to twist each handle at the same time, firmly, as you roll it against the direction of hair growth. When it&#x27;s working, you&#x27;ll feel and see it gently grab all the hairs it can, slightly pulling your skin up as it goes. 3. It helps to puff up your face anywhere you can to make it more taut; the spring grabs the hair better that way. It&#x27;s not nearly as painful as waxing, for some reason (the only exception being the middle of the upper lip -- that was pretty intense). But that is the only negative thing I have to say, and we all pay a price for beauty, right?  I promise you will love it!</li>

    <li> I purchased the Bellabe from Amazon.com, prime shipping (yay, I love that) because I am a \\&quot;woman of a certain age\\&quot; with UBER sensitive skin who has never fared well with professional waxing. Figuring they can send people into space with MRE&#x27;s and a suction toilet, they should be able to make a tool to remove unwanted facial hair from the faces of \\&quot;women of a certain age.\\&quot;  Enter Bellabe Facial Hair Remover!  I read the reviews, all 970 of them, thereabouts, and heeded the advice given about the \\&quot;tougher hairs\\&quot; and the \\&quot;sensitive skin\\&quot; and the \\&quot;PAIN\\&quot; and I am here to tell you that this is NOTHING compared to the Epilady, this is FAR easier than that moment that you wait for the muslin wax strips to be ripped off your face and little blood spots to appear, and this is INFINATELY easier than natural childbirth. Put it in perspective folks.  Once you get the \\&quot;hang\\&quot; of twirling the handles in your little fingers to produce the torqueing action of the spring enough to actually pull hairs, it&#x27;s a breeze.  For the \\&quot;tougher hairs\\&quot; don&#x27;t curve the spring so much, level it out a little, twirl, then bend.  Might take a few tries, or just resort to the Medieval tweezer method for the die hard hairs.  My only words of caution would be... do NOT use this on eyebrows.  Possibly safe on the center bridge of the nose between the eyebrows but for God&#x27;s sake woman, keep that thing away from the actual eyebrows and eyelashes.  Also, those little frizzy sideburn hairs... clip those back or you will be sorry.  You do NOT want to be the woman in urgent care who is referred to as \\&quot;Need spring removal from eyelashes STAT!\\&quot; I love this little tool and just saying that makes my husband jealous.  Now for my face care facts.  I thoroughly cleanse my sensitive skin with either the Simple facial cleansing wipes or Dove Unscented soap and water, being careful not to scrub too vigorously.  I make sure my skin is dry, paper towels work well.  I pull out the Bellabe and go to work in the mirror... with my reading glasses on naturally.  I know you are currently picturing Mrs. Doubtfire, I assure you I am far hotter than she.  Upon my first use, I did only my lip, at night, before going to bed.  I needed the \\&quot;beauty sleep\\&quot; to recover as I had no idea what the result would be as I could, in fact, wake up looking like Mrs. Doubtfire.  After using the tool, I soaked a cotton ball with hydrogen peroxide, probably the cheapest anti-infective on the market, and cleansed my upper lip with that thoroughly.  Then I put a small dab of antibiotic ointment on the area... and went to bed.  In the morning I couldn&#x27;t tell anything had been done to my upper lip.  That night, I continued with the chin and some fine downey hair on the lower jaw area.  Same cleansing routine before and after, and same result. The tool comes with cleaning instructions.  My tips are:  Get a clean, unused toothbrush.  Take one end of the Bellabe between your teeth and pull the Bellabe slightly with the other hand to stretch it out only slightly.  With the remaining hand, take the clean toothbrush and brush the spring out on all sides.  Clean the toothbrush with alcohol or whatever, and allow to dry for the next cleaning.
